  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Apollo needs help, and he can think of only one place to go... an enclave of modern demigods known as Camp Half-Blood.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627593129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11123643408376242004"><blockquote>
  <i>Zeus needed someone to blame, so of course he’d picked the handsomest, most talented, most popular god in the pantheon: me.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>This might be my favourite Riordan book</b>. <br/><br/>I was actually disappointed with his last one - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_' title='The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sword of Summer</a> - and I began to question in my review if it was finally time for Mr. R. to take a step back from these books about Greek, Roman and Egyptian gods. The conflicts were similar and the teen "voices" had begun to blend into one. Magnus Chase could just as easily have</span>
  <span id="freeText11123643408376242004" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Zeus needed someone to blame, so of course he’d picked the handsomest, most talented, most popular god in the pantheon: me.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>This might be my favourite Riordan book</b>. <br /><br />I was actually disappointed with his last one - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_" title="The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Summer</a> - and I began to question in my review if it was finally time for Mr. R. to take a step back from these books about Greek, Roman and Egyptian gods. The conflicts were similar and the teen "voices" had begun to blend into one. Magnus Chase could just as easily have been Percy Jackson.<br /><br />BUT then RR had to throw Apollo into the mix. Apollo stands out because he is not a teenage boy. Well... technically, he *is* in this book. But he's actually an age-old immortal who has been cast out of Olympus by Zeus and turned into a regular human teenager. His voice, however, not to mention his snark and humour, are that of a <b>selfish, narcissistic, hilarious asshole</b>.<br /><br />Truly, this book is so refreshing! Apollo doesn't even pretend he's a do-gooder; in fact, it's clear from the beginning that he's out for himself and views humans as "meat sacks". Imagine his horror when he discovers that not only is he human, but he also has acne and flab. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Is anything sadder than the sound of a god hitting a pile of garbage bags?</i>
</blockquote><br />Of course, there's a whole lot of godly drama going on too. You don't get to be an old god like Apollo without making a LOT of enemies. But this mostly stood out to me as being <b>the funniest book Riordan has written</b> and that's really saying something, given that all his books are defined by his trademark snarky humour. Pure entertainment.<br /><br /><b>Apollo is the Gilderoy Lockhart of this world and it is hilarious</b>. There's a nice bit of schadenfreude to be had when this self-obsessed god finally gets what he deserves and has to rely on Percy Jackson for help. And yet, there is something undeniably lovable about him too. <br /><br />On that note, many familiar characters come in and out of this book. You don't have to have read the other books to understand and enjoy this one, but it does contain spoilers for the main series and the characters. <br /><br />This, for me, stood out amid a sea of similar stories and characters. I'm still not 100% sure I would want to read any more books that focus on teenage demigods (we've kind of been there and done that, in my opinion), but I will definitely see Apollo's story through to the end.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>It warmed my heart that my children had the right priorities: their skills, their images, their views on YouTube.</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11123643408376242004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394786091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7642526033207035574"><blockquote>
  <i>"Is anything sadder than the sound of a god hitting a pile of garbage bags?"</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Or to paraphrase, is there anything sadder than your <b>favorite author becoming a sellout?</b><br/><br/>It's blatantly obvious Riordan isn't even trying anymore. He knows he can put out a steaming heap of crap and Percy fangirls and Solangelo diehards would still be clawing over each other for a copy, sending This Hidden Disappointment to the top of the NYT bestseller's list.<br/><br/>I don't understand Solangelo—Will and Nico. They never had</span>
  <span id="freeText7642526033207035574" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Is anything sadder than the sound of a god hitting a pile of garbage bags?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Or to paraphrase, is there anything sadder than your <b>favorite author becoming a sellout?</b><br><br>It's blatantly obvious Riordan isn't even trying anymore. He knows he can put out a steaming heap of crap and Percy fangirls and Solangelo diehards would still be clawing over each other for a copy, sending This Hidden Disappointment to the top of the NYT bestseller's list.<br><br>I don't understand Solangelo—Will and Nico. They never had chemistry. They were slapped together in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18705209.The_Blood_of_Olympus__The_Heroes_of_Olympus___5_" title="The Blood of Olympus (The Heroes of Olympus, #5) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blood of Olympus</a> for the sole purpose of Nico getting over Percy. Yeah, it was sweet then and I was drunk on the magic of the finale, but their relationship is never fleshed out. They're presented as this oh-so-cute couple and we're automatically supposed to be on-board because they're gay.<br><br>To that, I say:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445789163ra/16703340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We ship Percy and Annabeth because they have <i>history.</i> They went to hell and back for each other. Their relationship weathered problems, like Luke and Rachel. They work so incredibly well as a couple and a team as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12127810.The_House_of_Hades__The_Heroes_of_Olympus___4_" title="The House of Hades (The Heroes of Olympus, #4) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of Hades</a> demonstrated.<br><br>What do Will and Nico have? A few conversations behind the Hades cabin. I expected their relationship to develop more in The Hidden Oracle, not a simple PSA about LGBTQIA rights from Riordan through Apollo. I'm glad we're seeing more diversity in campers, with Chinese and Brazilian demigods, but the way they're presented feels like a big neon sign flashing, "Look how inclusive I'm being!"<br><br>Solangelo isn't the problem. I can live with them and the obvious fanservice in the form of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Leo <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and Percy's reappearance. Props on ushering the son of Poseidon out of the story early, so Apollo and new characters can shine. <br><br>(I was dying to use that pun.)<br><br><b>But the fucking plot.</b> It was formulaic and recycled and I can feel angry tears springing to my eyes as I type this. I can bitch and whine about Riordan not leaving Percy in peace, but I grudgingly and eagerly accept new series <b>as long as he kept delivering quality content.</b> <br><br>The pacing of Apollo's character arc can be described by one word: whiplash. Too fast, too out of the blue. The <b>writing itself has regressed.</b> For the first time, I feel like I'm reading middle grade. Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians had the occasional beautiful sentence, and the Heroes of Olympus showed leaps and bounds in prose. The Hidden Oracle is filled with short, simple sentences and quickly dated popculture references. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["You don't want to wake the Beast," is a shameless ripoff of Game of Thrones.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Its predecessors knew when to put a lid on the enchilada jokes and get serious. Percy's fight with Ares way back in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_" title="The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a> was dead serious. The grand climax of The Hidden Oracle is frankly ridiculous. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The statue sneezes his head off, for fuck's sake. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Rhea portrayed as a tree-hugging hippie is a tired Riordan stereotype. Yes, mighty gods are door-to-door salesman and hobos. Call me when it's 2005 again. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465655233ra/19385857.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there's Meg, the demigod that claims Apollo into her service—and obligatory female partner-in-crime, like Annabeth or Sam from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_" title="The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Summer</a>. She's a bratty, more annoying version of your typical Strong Female Character. One that doesn't have a lot of personality, but she can fight and backsass, so that automatically makes her the face of feminism.<br><br>I wouldn't be as peeved had Riordan not shown himself <b>capable of creating more complex female characters.</b> Reyna is a goddess. Her character arc in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18705209.The_Blood_of_Olympus__The_Heroes_of_Olympus___5_" title="The Blood of Olympus (The Heroes of Olympus, #5) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blood of Olympus</a> was one of the highlights of the whole book. She got rejected by both Jason <i>and</i> Percy, but sucked it up to fight a war. She became allies with their girlfriends and eventually friends. She sought to bridge the Greek and Roman camps, even though she had every reason to hate them. She doesn't magically find a boyfriend to mend her broken heart in the end and gets over it through time and space. <br><br>I officially ship Reyna with herself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465655233ra/19385858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've loved Percy and his adventures for nearly 8 years. I lived through the movie announcement, then subsequent disappointment at the actual product. My edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_" title="The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a> isn't even in print anymore.<br><br>I'm as big as a fan as before. All I'm asking for a little respect. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431103203ra/14792254.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1659243870" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Dark Prophecy</a><br><br><b>Pre-review: </b><br><br>Cynical Natalie: *grumbles* Not another one. <br><br>Nice Natalie: OH MY GOD IT'S ABOUT APOLLO MAYBE IT'LL BE IN HIS POV I CAN'T BREATHE <br><br>Cynical Natalie: Stop it, stop it! Don't you see this is another attempt to squeeze money out of the Percy Jackson series? How can he prove himself a relevant writer if he keeps writing the same thing?<br><br>Nice Natalie: SQUEEEEE WE CAN SEE PERCY<br><br>Cynical Natalie: You didn't hear a word I said, did you?<br><br>Nice Natalie: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444179961ra/16463495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cynical Natalie: We've lost her.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7642526033207035574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672582304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer778533245658962721"><strong>3.5 stars</strong><br/><br/><strong> </strong>Yesterday, he was the mighty and melodious Apollo, son of Zeus. Today, he is Lester Papadopoulos, a mere, ungifted mortal.<br/><br/>There’s only one thing for him to do now: join the demigods at Camp Half-Blood.<br/><br/>What makes <em>The Hidden Oracle</em> incredibly interesting is Apollo himself. Yes, he is one narcissistic personage with high standards and a peculiar appreciation for poetry.<br/><br/>And, yes, he is tremendously flawed, there is no denying that. But funnily enough, that’s what makes him so likeable.<br/><br/>Plus</span>
  <span id="freeText778533245658962721" style="display:none"><strong>3.5 stars</strong><br /><br /><strong> </strong>Yesterday, he was the mighty and melodious Apollo, son of Zeus. Today, he is Lester Papadopoulos, a mere, ungifted mortal.<br /><br />There’s only one thing for him to do now: join the demigods at Camp Half-Blood.<br /><br />What makes <em>The Hidden Oracle</em> incredibly interesting is Apollo himself. Yes, he is one narcissistic personage with high standards and a peculiar appreciation for poetry.<br /><br />And, yes, he is tremendously flawed, there is no denying that. But funnily enough, that’s what makes him so likeable.<br /><br />Plus, there is nothing more endearing than seeing a god care for his half-human offspring. Apollo is very protective when it comes to his children and friends.<br /><br />No one can say that he only cares about himself.<br /><br />As usual with any Rick Riordan book, <em>The Hidden Oracle</em> is filled with adventure, action, danger, mythology, monstrous creatures, originality, friendship and fun moments!<br /><br />My qualm? It acts too much as the spin-off to <em>The Heroes of Olympus</em>, which is a series I could not bring myself to finish.<br /><br />It can be read without having any knowledge of the aforementioned series, but there are countless of mentions of characters from it—many are actually part of this new series as well.<br /><br />My suggestion is that you at least read the first book in <em>The Heroes of Olympus</em> if you have the time, for the author does not present the old characters in grand detail; he basically assumes we are already acquainted with them.<br /><br /><em>The Hidden Oracle</em> is a highly entertaining new series containing a large set of characters and many adventures. It plunges the god of music, prophecy and healing, Apollo, into a dozen cut-throat situations.<br /><br />I read it in a single day and look extremely forward to the sequel.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1411661370" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411661370" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411661370?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411661370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11127755221885808239"><blockquote>
  <i>“Things can turn out differently, Apollo. That's the nice thing about being human. We only have one life, but we can choose what kind of story it's going to be.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Dammit, Rick Riordan. <b>This book was actually really good.</b> WHAT THE HELL. <br/><br/>When I first heard about <i>Trials of Apollo</i>, I had very mixed feelings. On one hand I felt like, “Jeez Rick, please don’t turn into a huge sell-out.” On the other hand, I was like, “I GET TO BE REUNITED WITH ALL THE PJO/HOO CHARACTERS YET AGAIN!! YESSSS.”<br/><br/>Honestly,</span>
  <span id="freeText11127755221885808239" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Things can turn out differently, Apollo. That's the nice thing about being human. We only have one life, but we can choose what kind of story it's going to be.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Dammit, Rick Riordan. <b>This book was actually really good.</b> WHAT THE HELL. <br><br>When I first heard about <i>Trials of Apollo</i>, I had very mixed feelings. On one hand I felt like, “Jeez Rick, please don’t turn into a huge sell-out.” On the other hand, I was like, “I GET TO BE REUNITED WITH ALL THE PJO/HOO CHARACTERS YET AGAIN!! YESSSS.”<br><br>Honestly, the premise––which is that Apollo turns mortal (a punishment from Zeus) and has to attend Camp Half-Blood––sounds like someone’s fanfiction idea or something. So I was a little like, “Oh boy, how is this going to last for an entire book––an entire <i>five-book series</i> for that matter?”<br><br>I guess I can only speak for the first book so far, but <b>somehow it works.</b> I was honestly just going to read this book for kicks––and to find out what had happened to certain PJO/HoO characters. But I ended up being way more invested in the story than I thought I would be. <b>Not only is this book good, but I seriously think it’s the best thing Rick Riordan has written in the past few years.</b> I liked this book more than <i>Magnus Chase</i> and honestly I think I liked it more than <i>Blood of Olympus</i> as well. <br><br><b>
  <u>What I liked:</u>
</b><br><br><b>Apollo’s narration.</b> Oh my goodness, it’s hilarious. I always loved Apollo in the PJO books, and it’s amazing to get to read a whole story in his perspective. Somehow he manages to be super conceited but also so lovable at the same time? And I think it’s because we all know he actually has a heart, hidden underneath all that vanity. <br><br>But also, it’s hilarious to see him trying to adjust to being mortal. Oh, and I loved that all the chapter titles were haikus. <br><br><b>It’s not a journey story.</b> I think this may be the first ever Rick Riordan book where the characters don’t go on an epic quest. Not that I don’t mind a good journey story, but I was relieved this book didn’t follow the typical Riordan formula.<br><br>This is where <i>The Kane Chronicles</i> and <i>Magnus Chase</i>, and even <i>Heroes of Olympus</i> fell a little flat for me––I liked them, but it was starting to feel like the same story over and over again: “the characters go on some long journey, they meet a bunch of quirky mythological beings along the way!” <br><br><i>The Hidden Oracle</i>, on the other hand, mostly just takes place at Camp Half-Blood. Yet, there is still tension, mystery, and conflict without the characters having to wander all over the country. Towards the end, I got the sense it was setting up for a journey story in the next book(s), but I at least appreciate that Rick stepped out of his comfort zone for this first installment. <br><br><b>Percy Jackson gets a freakin’ break.</b> I was excited Percy was in this book, of course (and I found it hilarious that Meg immediately has a crush on him––oh my god, everyone is in love with this kid). But I also liked that Percy didn’t stick around for the whole book (as much as I love him). He’s just like, “Look, I’ll give you a ride to camp and I’ll check in this weekend––but I also have a life and stuff.” I’m sure he’ll get dragged into more shenanigans in this series, but I’m also glad to see him trying to live a normal life––trying to catch up on schoolwork, thinking about college, etc. <b>#LetPercyLive2k16</b> <br><br><b>The humor.</b> Rick really brought it with the humor in this one––I haven’t laughed so much at a book in a long time. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Then the glow become brighter: a holographic golden sickle with a few sheaves of wheat, rotating just above Meg McCaffrey.<br><br>A boy in the crowd gasped. “She's a communist!”<br><br>A girl who'd been sitting at Cabin Four's table gave him a disgusted sneer. “No, Damien, that's my mom's symbol.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Just … oh my gosh. *dies of laughter* <br><br><b>MEG.</b> I love Meg. I love that she wears glasses and eats a lot and has a little bit of hair above her upper lip. I love that she’s a daughter of Demeter, and that being a child of the harvest/agriculture goddess is actually portrayed as being pretty badass. I love how endearingly odd she is. I love that she gets to be an important part of the story, when most of the time a similar character would have to take the sidelines.<br><br><b>I also love the friendship between Meg and Apollo.</b> He starts off thinking she’s a total nuisance and then ends up really caring about her in the end, and just … mY HEART. <br><br><b>THE SOLANGELO.</b> OH MY GOD. OH. MY. GOD. I was grinning my head off about these two throughout the whole book. I am ridiculously happy to finally see a canon gay couple in one of Riordan’s books, and it was worth the wait. These two are PERFECT, OMFG.<br><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Will put his hand on Nico's shoulder. "Nico, we need to have another talk about your people skills."<br><br>"Hey, I'm just stating the obvious. If this is Apollo, and he dies, we're all in trouble."<br><br>Will turned to me. "I apologize for my boyfriend."<br><br>Nico rolled his eyes. "Could you not―"<br><br>"Would you prefer special guy?" Will asked. "Or significant other?"<br><br>"Significant annoyance, in your case," Nico grumbled.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><i>BOYFRIEND.</i> HE SAID BOYFRIEND.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Nico," I said at last, "shouldn't you be sitting at the Hades table?"<br><br>He shrugged. "Technically, yes. But if I sit alone at my table, strange things happen. Cracks open in the floor. Zombies crawl out and start roaming around. It's a mood disorder. I can't control it. That's what I told Chiron. "<br><br>"And is it true?" I asked.<br><br>Nico smiled thinly. "I have a note from my doctor."<br><br>Will raised his hand. "I'm his doctor."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>CAN YOU HEAR ME SCREAMING. THESE TWO DORKS. I CAN’T HANDLE IT.<br><br>And you know what I also love? <b>I love that Apollo is so open about being bisexual.</b> Honestly this just means so, so much to me. The first time Apollo mentioned that his two true loves had been Daphne and Hyacinthus my jaw kinda dropped, because I really hadn’t expected Rick Riordan to acknowledge that.<br><br>And I was already happy with that one little nod to Apollo’s sexuality, but <i>it doesn’t end there</i>. Apollo clearly states at one point that he has been in relationships with numerous men and women, and throughout the story he notes the attractiveness of both male and female characters. I had expected that at most Rick Riordan would <i>hint</i> that Apollo was bisexual, so I was just overjoyed that he didn’t try to hide it at all. <br><br>In all seriousness, this representation means a lot to me. There were no LGBTQIA characters in the books I read as a kid. <i>None.</i> I don’t think I saw queer characters in a book until I was like 15. So to see a book like this, where there is both a canon gay couple and a bisexual protagonist, and to know that gay and bisexual kids could grow up reading this book/series and actually feel represented … that gives me so many feelings. I wish I’d had this kind of representation when I was a kid.<br><br><b>
  <u>What didn’t work for me:</u>
</b><br><br>As I said, I did appreciate that this book took things a little more slowly than most of Riordan’s books. However, <b>I did wish there’d been a <i>little</i> bit more going on</b>. The whole book felt like it was building up to something bigger––which isn’t necessarily a bad thing, but it also made it feel a little incomplete. <br><br><b>The references to modern technology.</b> Look, I know Rick Riordan wants to appeal to the cool kids and all, but at times I found this a little cringe-worthy. All the references to things like Skype, YouTube, Snapchat, etc. tend to feel forced and unnecessary to me––not only that, but they’re probably going to seem silly and obsolete to any kid who reads this book in ten years. <br><br><b>There was a major plot twist I was a little iffy about.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m talking about the whole thing where Meg (sort of) betrays Apollo. It was a tad clichéd and I was slightly disappointed that Riordan took it that route … I just feel like the same plotline has been done a million times. However, I did like that it added more depth to her character. It’s pretty messed up how much Nero has manipulated and emotionally abused her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <u>The final word:</u>
</b><br><br>This book really came out of left field for me. I had lost a bit of faith in Rick Riordan over the past few years, but I feel like he redeemed himself with this one. I was initially anxious about yet another PJO spin-off, but now I’m finding myself really excited about it. <br><br>I love Apollo’s narration. I love the humor. I love the new characters and I love seeing the old characters again. <br><br>I guess I’ll be reading this series until I’m like 30. <i>Dammit, Rick.</i><br><br>(Pre-release ranting/fangirling under the cut.)<br><br>---------<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>2/11/16:</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455215821i/18074954._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/560551.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WELP, THAT'S IT. I'M SOLD. <br><br>----------<br><br><b>12/10/15:</b><br><br>YESSSS, MORE INFO. <br><br>- First of all, we have a book cover now! OOOOOH, pretty. <br>- Apparently this is going to be a <b>5 book series</b>. ... Which means I'm literally going to be almost 30 by the time the last book comes out. That's a scary thought. <br>- Most importantly, <b>PERCY IS IN IT. THIS IS NOT A DRILL.</b> <br>- You can read a short excerpt from the book <a href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/life/books/2015/12/10/rick-riordan-exclusive-excerpt-the-trials-of-apollo-percy-jackson/76780734/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. <br><br>----------<br><br><b>10/8/15:</b><br><br>Oh boy. I know I shouldn't be excited for this. I know Rick Riordan is just milking the Percy Jacskon franchise for all it's worth. I know he's essentially just writing fanfiction of his own series at this point.<br><br>AND YET ...... I don't care, honestly. And despite what the rational side of me says, I <i>am</i> excited. Because:<br><br>- Apollo's point of view is sure to be hilarious.<br>- I'm just imagining Apollo trying to adjust to Camp Half-Blood life and it's glorious.<br>- Heroes of Olympus left a bunch of loose ends and I want to know what happens. <br>- WE GET TO SEE ALL THE OLD CHARACTERS AGAIN??????!!!!! <s>WE GET MORE PERCABETH??!!?! WE GET TO SEE NICO AND WILL AS A COUPLE HOPEFULLY???!!!!</s><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/395314.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1410727890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410727890" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410727890?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=slow">slow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410727890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3893261471860851906">1. 5 stars<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464191987i/19210853.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464191904ra/19210819.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <u>A Tired Spin on the Same Old Formula</u>
</b><br/>I’ll be perfectly blunt: <i>you don’t look to Riordan for originality</i>. We all know this to be true. Hell, the very first Percy Jackson books rode the Harry Potter-ripoff wave to C-List stardom and even then he just rewrote ancient myths in a modern format. Now he’s going back to his roots and just ripping off his previous stories under that hypnotic guise of nostalgia. We return to Camp Half-Blood <s>Prince</s> and meet some familiar characters like *Percy</span>
  <span id="freeText3893261471860851906" style="display:none">1. 5 stars<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464191987i/19210853.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464191904ra/19210819.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>A Tired Spin on the Same Old Formula</u>
</b><br>I’ll be perfectly blunt: <i>you don’t look to Riordan for originality</i>. We all know this to be true. Hell, the very first Percy Jackson books rode the Harry Potter-ripoff wave to C-List stardom and even then he just rewrote ancient myths in a modern format. Now he’s going back to his roots and just ripping off his previous stories under that hypnotic guise of nostalgia. We return to Camp Half-Blood <s>Prince</s> and meet some familiar characters like *Percy and Nico, only to go on the same old adventures.<br><br>The main difference here is that Apollo has been stripped of his godly powers and must face a road to redemption instead of just being a godly offspring. This theme, again, is heavily borrowed from pre-existing mythology.<br><br>*Percy’s return is a mirror of Annabeth’s in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067355764?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Sword of Summer</i>
</a>--which leads me to believe that since these two series are released near each other and seem to have the same timeline that they will at some point (at least partially) intersect. But Percy’s reappearance being very much like his girlfriend’s before him again shows that Riordan is running out of fresh material and reusing his own plots.<br><br><b>Cringey Dad Jokes: Mythology Edition</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464191904i/19210820._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>*SMH* Rick writes Apollo in his own voice: <i>desperately unhip yet trying way too effing hard to be cool.</i> And completely oblivious to this fact as a writer. His references are outdated and will go over the heads of the target Middle Grade audience. They won’t get the mess that was the 2007 Britney Spears VMA performance unless they care enough to google it—because they either weren’t born at the time or were watching cartoons instead. And this is something that is mentioned on page one, yet the whole book is littered with these gems.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464191904i/19210821._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>^This is also the basis of Riordan’s books: The gods got <i>bizay</i> with mortals. So it comes [pun intended] as no surprise that Apollo has had many lovers, both female and male—a fact that Riordan seems to hammer [yep, still punnin’] home at every possible chance to prove how hip both he and Apollo are with teh ghey stuff when he finds out his son has a boyfriend. This is peak Riordan dad joke cringe right here, because he continually beats [heh punz] this long dead horse way past trying to make any point that he’s so kewl with it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464191904i/19210822.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If that wasn’t bad enough, each chapter heading has increasingly lame haikus over them. I feel like this whole book could have used a good editor to show Riordan that so much of it is just cringey or trite; but according to a source with the same publisher, they just don’t care about quality and expect the author to do it all. I guess Riordan in his utmost dweebiness thought this was a good effort, then again, he also chose this as his book jacket picture:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464191904i/19210823.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(No, seriously. This guy thought ^this^ was a flattering pic. Yikes.)<br><br>The villain here is laughably melodramatic, and not in a good way. It’s like watching Bailee Madison in basically any of her roles, just chewing the scenery and not believable at all. (Honestly, how the hell does that annoying actress get roles?! She has no talent whatsoever)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464191904ra/19210824.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3893261471860851906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2169367563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8063854150141286606"><b>5 Golden Stars</b><br/>not complete but 98%<br/><br/><br/><b>READERS ATTENTION!:</b><br/><i>before starting this series, you should have read these:<br/>first, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40736-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians' rel='nofollow noopener'>Percy Jackson</a><br/>then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/51379-heroes-of-olympus' rel='nofollow noopener'> Heroes of Olympus </a><br/>Also Trials of Apollo is happening at the same time with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/82212-magnus-chase-and-the-gods-of-asgard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magnus Chase</a>; they have crossovers sometimes.<br/>(or if it's hard to remember go here & read in this order: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/183923-camp-half-blood-chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Camp Half-Blood Chronicles</a>)</i><br/>I literally warned everywhere I could, so I should've put it in my review too. :D<br/><br/><br/>now<br/>*clapping my hands*<br/>where were we?<br/>Trials of Apollo, Book 1: the Hidden Oracl</span>
  <span id="freeText8063854150141286606" style="display:none"><b>5 Golden Stars</b><br />not complete but 98%<br /><br /><br /><b>READERS ATTENTION!:</b><br /><i>before starting this series, you should have read these:<br />first, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40736-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians" rel="nofollow noopener">Percy Jackson</a><br />then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51379-heroes-of-olympus" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heroes of Olympus </a><br />Also Trials of Apollo is happening at the same time with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/82212-magnus-chase-and-the-gods-of-asgard" rel="nofollow noopener">Magnus Chase</a>; they have crossovers sometimes.<br />(or if it's hard to remember go here &amp; read in this order: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/183923-camp-half-blood-chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">Camp Half-Blood Chronicles</a>)</i><br />I literally warned everywhere I could, so I should've put it in my review too. :D<br /><br /><br />now<br />*clapping my hands*<br />where were we?<br />Trials of Apollo, Book 1: the Hidden Oracle<br />yessss!<br /><br />I loved this book.<br />so much fun!<br />Solangelo! (my other OTP) <i>I want more! I NEED more!</i><br />thrills &amp; feels (not so tense but I'm so emotional)<br />the first part was the funniest!<br />the last part was the best! (&amp; funny too, you can't expect Apollo's narration not to be fun! XD)<br />&amp; the COVER is GORGEOUS! OMG! *mesmerizing with the beauty*<br /><br />I always loved Apollo in Greek mythology (before reading Percy Jackson) &amp; he is awesome in this world of modern Greek mythology retelling, Camp Halfblood &amp; Demigods too! I love we have a series about him. :)<br />he is completely a DRAMA QUEEN (he even approved himself as a dramatic god somewhere in his haiku.)<br />Of course he was a whining wimpy Narcissistic (sometimes idiot) character at first (&amp; that was funny!) he was an immortal punished to be a mortal; those are very different states...<br /><br /><br /><i>How do you punish a powerful immortal??<br /><br />By making him powerless &amp; mortal</i><br /><br /><br />but he started to change soon.<br />He stood up for his mission, because he believed that was something he must have done himself:<br /><br />he changed from this:<br /><i>I would rather have pick a nice group of heroes &amp; sent them...</i><br />to this:<br /><i>"I won't allow any others to put themselves at risk."</i><br /><br />My heart melted when he was singing; like I could actually hear him told his stories, his remorse. He accepted he made mistakes.<br />He actually changed:<br /><br /><i>✦ besides, I thought, I don't want to risk losing you again.<br />✦ "I risked my life for you," I said in amazement. "and that actually means something. because I can die!"</i><br /><br />&amp; as Percy said at nearly the end; to his statement of<br />"gods do not change and grow and mature."<br /><br /><i>✦ "You sure about that? You seemed pretty different to me."</i><br /><br />Also meeting his children was one of the fantastic moments of the book! (&amp; funny ofc)<br />&amp; I loved to see some of the older familiar (favourite) characters is back in this series! I wish we see others too!<br />and the good feeling of rushing adrenaline through my veins inside the pages! (even after 3rd re-read) I love the excitements! it makes me feel alive.<br /><br />at the end, He still whines but as long as he cares &amp; sometimes acting courageously, doesn't matter he thinks like a crybaby. also his whining brings more fun to the story. XD<br />I can understand him.<br /><br /><i>Bless Riordan's writing style! </i>Seems so <i>real</i>, all the characters &amp; events; I think sometimes Apollo &amp; his haikus &amp; Percy &amp; his friends might really exist &amp; world came to an ending twice! (that's insane, I know!)<br /><br /><br />p.s. I want to eat tortillas with seven layered dip &amp; blue cookies! am I the only one!?<br />p.s. 2. the only thing I didn't like much was Myrmekes. (because I don't like bugs.)<br />p.s. 3. I think I can say Riordan is a Supernatural fan.<br />-<br />World building: ★★★★★/5<br />Characters: ★★★★★/5<br />/ Characters development: ★★★★★/5<br />Written style: ★★★★★/5<br />/ Fun: ★★★★★/5<br />/ Feelz: ★★★★★/5<br />Plot: ★★★★/5<br />General idea: ★★★★★/5</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410880785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1679266229346174470"><b>
  <blockquote>The others seemed confused. Then the glow became brighter: a holographic golden sickle with a few sheaves of wheat, rotating just above Meg McCaffrey.<br/><br/>A boy in the crowd gasped. “She’s a communist!”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462802933i/19045853.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Hidden Oracle continues right after The Blood of Olympus. Apollo aka Lester Papadopoulos is banished from Olympus. He used to be a god, when he's mortal, he doesn't have his power and that makes him very upset. In this book, you will meet the same old characters such as Percy, Nico, Chiron and </span>
  <span id="freeText1679266229346174470" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>The others seemed confused. Then the glow became brighter: a holographic golden sickle with a few sheaves of wheat, rotating just above Meg McCaffrey.<br><br>A boy in the crowd gasped. “She’s a communist!”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462802933i/19045853.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Hidden Oracle continues right after The Blood of Olympus. Apollo aka Lester Papadopoulos is banished from Olympus. He used to be a god, when he's mortal, he doesn't have his power and that makes him very upset. In this book, you will meet the same old characters such as Percy, Nico, Chiron and Will. If you love Nico and Will being together, this book won't disappoint you. If you miss Percy and want to see him once again, this book will bring you joy. So The Hidden Oracle is for the fans who always want more of Rick Riordan's stories, the world of Percy Jackson and Greek gods.<br><br>Apollo is a remarkable character from the first page. Rick Riordan pulled me into the story easily as if there was magic in it when I touched the book and it told me that: 'Love me ! Reading me is so fun and don't put me down'. So it turned out that I couldn't put it down for hours and had to read until I finished it. Rick ! You hooked me to this stuff (again). I love The Hidden Apollo more than The Blood of Olympus because I feel like this is a good start for the brand new stories to come. There's just one storyline and it doesn't tangle like it does in The Hero of Olympus series. The story is easy to understand and focus. Apollo always made me laugh and I enjoyed every moment of that. Even if when Percy appears on the scene, my focus shifted from Apollo to him, but it's not a problem. xD<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462804094ra/19045964.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“And I have acne,” I lamented. “And flab.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>This book is a bit better than Magnus Chase, however, I kinda like Magnus Chase even more. Maybe it's because I'm not excited about Greek gods anymore or so. Norse mythology is new for me, and I was super excited when I read Magnus Chase. Anyway, this book is great and the narrative is not boring at all - it's engaging and hilarious, the dynamic of the characters is abundant. There're four oracles waiting to be explored at the end of this book. I want to see Apollo's development in the next book and how hard he learns his lessons for both him and Meg. Can't wait !<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462804499ra/19046001.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://goo.gl/E0blSX">http://goo.gl/E0blSX</a></span>

<div id="review_2194581346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194581346" />
    <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz"><img alt="Ahmed  Ejaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598778737p2/53694260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194581346?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed  Ejaz" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz">Ahmed  Ejaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=full-lengths">full-lengths</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194581346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16587681238784171178"><b>
  <i>I remember when I started this book last year</i>
</b> without reading the previous ten books, one of my best friends here told me I have to read previous books. I was sad because I had read, I think, 5 chapters or so and I was quite enjoying it. And reading ten whole books seemed a huge mess to me. Now I understood that my friend was right.<br/>**Thank you, if you are reading this review. :)**<br/> <br/>>>The book started off in an excellent manner. Very much interesting. It was so hilarious how Apollo was, litera</span>
  <span id="freeText16587681238784171178" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>I remember when I started this book last year</i>
</b> without reading the previous ten books, one of my best friends here told me I have to read previous books. I was sad because I had read, I think, 5 chapters or so and I was quite enjoying it. And reading ten whole books seemed a huge mess to me. Now I understood that my friend was right.<br />**Thank you, if you are reading this review. :)**<br /> <br />&gt;&gt;The book started off in an excellent manner. Very much interesting. It was so hilarious how Apollo was, literally, whining about him being a mere mortal. Jokes aside, I enjoyed his whining. Does it seem cold? Then be it! :D<br />&gt;&gt;We got a whole bunch of new characters. Especially, Meg was a good one. We didn't get much of her past. Really looking forward to read more of her. By the way, I had guessed her godly parent before revelation. I know I won't be getting award for this as it was obvious.<br />&gt;&gt;We get a new, maybe, Great prophecy here. It's totally different from the ones we have read previously. I liked it. But still my favourite prophecy is The Prophecy of Seven. <br />&gt;&gt;Rhea! Wow! Her entrance was...OMG! I loved her meeting with Apollo. <br />&gt;&gt;Now Uncle Rick is, brilliantly, trying to link the previous events with a company of three roman emperors. Well, I wasn't interested in it because it seemed too much. But eventually it all made sense. <br /><br />One thing I would mention that this book seemed boring to me at some points in the middle. Really! Maybe it was not boring? I just felt it that way because I am reading his books almost in row? <br />I pretty much liked this book. But I think previous ten books in the series are better than this. Maybe because this is just the beginning. I just can't say it, but something feels off. Really hope next book will be amazing.<br /><br />🌟🌟<b>4.50 Stars</b>🌟🌟<br /><br />7 December, 2017</span>
  <a data-text-id="16587681238784171178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText6036367577659087856" style="display:none">The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo #1), Rick Riordan<br /><br />The Hidden Oracle is a fantasy novel based on Greek and Roman mythology written by Rick Riordan. It was published on May 3, 2016, and is the first book in The Trials of Apollo series, the second spin-off of the Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians series. <br /><br />The book follows the god Apollo, who is turned into a human teenager and thrown down from Olympus to New York City as a punishment by his father Zeus. Apollo goes to Camp Half-Blood, where he discovers that he will have to regain control of the five oracles of Ancient Greece in order to receive pardon from Zeus.<br /><br />عنوانها: پیشگویی پنهان؛ آپولو: پیشگویی پنهان؛ نویسنده: ریک ریوردان؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و ششم ماه مارس سال 2016 میلادی<br />عنوان: پیشگویی پنهان؛ نویسنده: ریک ریوردان؛ مترجم: فرزام حبیبی اصفهانی؛ تهران، آریابان، 1395، در 347 ص؛ شابک 9789647196659؛ <br /><br />عنوان: آپولو: پیشگویی پنهان؛ نویسنده: ریک ریوردان؛ مترجم: آرزو مقدس؛ تهران، نشر پرتقال، 1396، در 400 ص؛ شابک 9786008675556؛ <br /><br />آپولو، یکی از ایزدان اُلمپ، چون پدرش زئوس را، خشمگین کرد، از اُلمپ بیرونش کردند، و به آدمیزاد بدل شد. حالا برای تنبیه، او به شکل یک پسر نوجوان، به شهر نیویورک، سقوط کرده، و باید، یاد بگیرد، چطور روی زمین، از خودش، مراقبت کند. آپولو، که دشمنان بسیار، هم در بین هیولاها، و دیوها، و هم بین ایزدان دارد، برای بازگشت به زادگاهش، باید کوشش کند، دوباره نظر زئوس را، جلب کند. اما بدون داشتن ت‌وانیهای ایزدی، و جاودانگی، اینکار چگونه باید به پایان برسد؟ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1389809726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389809726" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389809726?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141363912" href="/book/show/26881479-the-hidden-oracle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-without-romance">ya-without-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389809726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14036491508079941936">I've officially read 13 Camp Half Blood books and <b>I DON'T THINK I'LL EVER HAVE ENOUGH OF THEM.</b> This was <i>brilliant</i>. I laughed my head off at the perfectness of the humour and sass and basically Apollo's narcissism was <i>glorious</i>. TRULY GLORIOUS. And I particularly loved that this one didn't follow the general plot-themes of the other Riordan books. Like, okay, I totally can get onboard with a prophecy, a team, and a wild adventure. But it's refreshing to NOT have that for once??? SO YAY.<br/><br/><b>WHAT TO EXP</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14036491508079941936" style="display:none">I've officially read 13 Camp Half Blood books and <b>I DON'T THINK I'LL EVER HAVE ENOUGH OF THEM.</b> This was <i>brilliant</i>. I laughed my head off at the perfectness of the humour and sass and basically Apollo's narcissism was <i>glorious</i>. TRULY GLORIOUS. And I particularly loved that this one didn't follow the general plot-themes of the other Riordan books. Like, okay, I totally can get onboard with a prophecy, a team, and a wild adventure. But it's refreshing to NOT have that for once??? SO YAY.<br /><br /><b>WHAT TO EXPECT IN THIS BOOK:</b><br />• The glorious god Apollo is now a mortal teenage boy with acne.<br />• Percy Jackson (!!!!) and I'd say he has <i>more</i> than a cameo because he's at the beginning and helps out in the finale too (!!!!)<br />• SO MUCH WITTY DIALOGUE IT'S GLORIOUS.<br />• So you'll laugh. All the time, probably.<br />• A stubborn 12-year-old girl claiming Apollo's servitude while he's mortal. Arguing ensues.<br />• Evil ants<br />• Plenty of people being lost / beaten up / stabbed / liked by lions<br />• Epic and obscure Greek mythology tales that I didn't know so dangit I learned stuff<br />• Peaches<br />• Really really really bad haikus<br /><br /><br /><b><u>****NOTE****</u> If you haven't read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7736182.The_Lost_Hero__The_Heroes_of_Olympus___1_" title="The Lost Hero (The Heroes of Olympus, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Hero</a> (Heroes of Olympus) series <u>DO NOT</u> read Trials of Apollo yet. You'll be thoroughly spoiled!!!</b><br /><br /><b>So of course I really loved Apollo.</b> He had a really different voice to Percy and Co, which was great. He almost spoke formally, like a god would, but also teenager-y. So it was just an epically hilarious combination. <b>Plus he was so full of himself.</b> It was <i>hilarious.</i> And, then he had an interesting relationship with <b>Meg</b>...like I did like Meg?? But I didn't actually feel like we got to know her so well. She was stubborn and opinionated and annoying. But I wanted MORE from her personality. (Also I totally predicted the Big Meg Plot Twist. So.) But I did love how it was gangly narcissistic Apollo teamed up with a 12 year old who blew raspberries at him when they fought. Levels of adorable = 110%<br /><br />Which leads me to also say: <b>NO ROMANCE!!</b> Apollo references / pines after some of his old loves, but honestly there is zilch romance here. So refreshing. (Oh, and it also indicates quite clearly that Apollo is bi!)<br /><br /><b>The plot, of course, had plenty of action.</b> It also had plenty of monologues. And I tend to get a bit turned off at Greek mythology monologues. I just....?? STRUGGLE TO CARE, I GUESS. So there were several parts where I wish <b>there had been less talking; more stabbing.</b> But I was VERY pleased this wasn't so enormous. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15724396.The_Sword_of_Summer__Magnus_Chase_and_the_Gods_of_Asgard___1_" title="The Sword of Summer (Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Summer</a> was waaaay too long tbh.<br /><br /><b>Also I freaking love Camp Half Blood but seriously, how is everyone not dead?</b> Literally EVERYTHING they do is a near-death experience and everyone's just like "Oh well" and then demi-gods get their arms chopped off or go missing or just die but whatever. It'll be right, mate. Everyone is just like "Oh don't wander over there YOU'LL DIE but we're roasting s'mores later on, be there!"<br /><br />I freaking love Camp Half Blood.<br /><br /><b>Also HELLO TO SOME OLD FAVOURITE CHARACTERS!!</b> Guess who's back?!?<br />• Rachel Dare (!!) the oracle from the first Percy Jackson series<br />• SOMEONE AWESOME I WON'T NAME BECAUSE OF SPOILERS BUT YUSSSSS<br />• Percy Jackson, like I said (sans Annabeth, she is actually at school, like, working)<br />• Nico (!!!) and his boyfriend Will (!!!) and they're SO CUTE and argue all the time. Although when in Hades are we going to get a NICO CENTRED SERIES??!? I WOULD ABSOLUTELY DIE OF HAPPINESS IF WE COULD. PLEASE GIVE THE LORD OF DARKNESS HIS OWN BOOKS!!! PLEEEEEASE!!. <br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: I enjoyed myself far too much, honestly.</b> I laughed (OUT LOUD) so many times. I fairly burst into pineapple fruitsalad of appreciation every time Percy Jackson appeared (&lt;3) and I loved the adventures and the near-death-experiences and the NEW EVIL in town. Love some new evil, tbh. Apollo is definitely one of my most favourite narrators ever and I need moooooore in this series. Definitely one of my favourites Riordan books!<br /><br /><br />*** QUOTES ***<br /><br /><blockquote>After being alive for so many millennia, I had trouble keep track of time even in the best of circumstances. I would hear a song on Spotify and think, <i>Oh, that's new!</i> Then I'd realise it was Mozart's Piano Concerto no. 20 in D Minor from two hundred years ago. Or I'd wonder why Herodotus the historian wasn't in my contacts list. Then I'd remember Herodotus didn't have a smartphone, because he had been dead since the Iron Age.<br />It's very irritating how quickly you mortals die.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Much to my disappointment, the Jacksons did not have a spare bow or quiver to lend me.<br />"I suck at archery," Percy explained.<br />"Yes, but <i>I</i> don't," I said. "This is why you should always plan for <i>my</i> needs."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote><i>Guardian?</i> Perhaps the spirit meant me. When in doubt, I usually assumed the conversation was about me.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I said a silent prayer that if I got through this race alive, I would sacrifice a bull to myself and possibly even build myself a new temple. I am a sucker for bulls and temples.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Are you all right?" I asked.<br />"Fine," she snapped.<br />Clearly that was not true. She looked as if she'd just gone through Hades's haunted house. (Pro tip: DO NOT.)</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I didn't understand the purpose of the seeds, but it was comforting to know that in a dire emergency I could hit people with my ukulele while Meg planted geraniums.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>[Villain talking] "There was a period of about three hundred years during the Middle Ages when my name was almost forgotten. I was little more than a mirage! Thank goodness for the Renaissance, when our Classical greatness was remembered. And then came the Internet. OH, gods, I <i>love</i> the internet! It is impossible for me to fade completely now. I am immortal on Wikipedia!"</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14036491508079941936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1701828965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701828965" />
    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398557569p2/10762033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_1412891724" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412891724" />
    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1412891724?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil (or bleed)" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed">Neil (or bleed)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=i-loved-it-aka-all-time-faves">i-loved-it-aka-all-time-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412891724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8000516369378986779"><blockquote>
  <i>"Nothing is more tragic than loving someone to the depths of your soul and knowing they cannot and will not ever love you back."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Time and time again, it has been proven that whenever I'm reading a Rick Riordan book, I read so fast that the words blurred. I mean, I can't stop flipping the goddamn pages like there's no tomorrow. Maybe, it's the humor or probably, something else.<br/><br/>Anyway...<br/><br/>The Hidden Oracle is... wait for it... an entertaining read. I don't say, right? Hahaha! If you loved PJO and</span>
  <span id="freeText8000516369378986779" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Nothing is more tragic than loving someone to the depths of your soul and knowing they cannot and will not ever love you back."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Time and time again, it has been proven that whenever I'm reading a Rick Riordan book, I read so fast that the words blurred. I mean, I can't stop flipping the goddamn pages like there's no tomorrow. Maybe, it's the humor or probably, something else.<br /><br />Anyway...<br /><br />The Hidden Oracle is... wait for it... an entertaining read. I don't say, right? Hahaha! If you loved PJO and HoO, you will definitely love this one, too. It has the same elements, the same aura with those books by Uncle Rick. Yet, The Hidden Oracle is also different in many ways.<br /><br />For the record, I like Apollo. I know he is selfish, a self-absorbed god and an asshole but his voice in this book made me like him. And his character development is superb. I liked how his character developed emotionally and intellectually. It fits and doesn't feel contrived at all. And don't forget his strong sarcasm and humor! *hands down*<br /><br />The interesting new set of demigods involved in this novel is so diverse and all cute, I mean, likable and adorable. I like their distinct voices and personalities and the genuine feelings they are propagating in my direction, either it's happiness or the opposite of it.<br /><br />We do have a great plot in this book. You know the drill, it involved prophecies and all but I still find it intriguing especially that it will scavenge other areas of Greek and Roman mythology.<br /><br />Finally, we've got to see again some of the familiar demigods we loved in the previous series OMG YES and got the answer we're waiting for! <br /><br />Can't wait to read the next book!!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8000516369378986779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1414777638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4838743081340699253"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462492069i/19004637._SY540_.jpg' width='564' height='564' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>After the not-so-successful Magnus Chase book, I know that some people are reluctant to go back to RR's world, but I'm here to tell ya.<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_' title='The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hidden Oracle</a> is so much better than The Sword of Summer. <br/><br/>Basically,this is the summary of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_' title='The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hidden Oracle</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462492069i/19004638.png' width='500' height='56' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book is different to the usual RR book and its formulatic story. Uncle Rick II is kinda famous for writing a book/series with demigods as main characters and though I love Percy and the gang, the characters and the plot are getting predictable. I'm</span>
  <span id="freeText4838743081340699253" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462492069i/19004637._SY540_.jpg" width="564" height="564" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After the not-so-successful Magnus Chase book, I know that some people are reluctant to go back to RR's world, but I'm here to tell ya.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a> is so much better than The Sword of Summer. <br><br>Basically,this is the summary of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462492069i/19004638.png" width="500" height="56" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is different to the usual RR book and its formulatic story. Uncle Rick II is kinda famous for writing a book/series with demigods as main characters and though I love Percy and the gang, the characters and the plot are getting predictable. I'm glad that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a> came something as a breathe of fresh air because we don't have a demigod hero in this book. What we have is a self-centered narcissistic ex-god who was turned into a human as a punishment.<br><br><i>MY NAME IS APOLLO. I used to be a god.</i><br><br>Apollo, the god of archery:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462492069ra/19004639.gif" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>is one of the funniest character that Uncle Rick II has created. His self-entitlement knows no boundaries and of all the heroes that Uncle Rick II has made in the past,Apollo is the least heroic character.<br><br><i>His chin was so weak I was tempted to create a GoFoundMe campaign to buy him a better jaw.</i><br><br>-Apollo<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462492069ra/19004640.gif" width="400" height="224" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, part of the reason why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a> is awesome is because Nico and Will (SolAngelo) is here. And. They. Are. <b>Goals.</b><br><br><i>Will put his hand on Nico’s shoulder. “Nico, we need to have another talk about your people<br>skills.”<br><br>“Hey, I’m just stating the obvious. If this is Apollo, and he dies, we’re all in trouble.”<br><br>Will turned to me. “I apologize for my boyfriend.”<br><br>Nico rolled his eyes. “Could you not—”<br><br>“Would you prefer special guy?” Will asked. “Or significant other?”<br><br>“Significant annoyance, in your case,” Nico grumbled.<br><br>“Oh, I’ll get you for that.”</i><br><br>Dying here. Omg.<br><br>And by the way,let us not forget my favorite Percy scene in this book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462492069i/19004641._SX540_.jpg" width="564" height="415" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and my favorite Percy quote:<br><br><i>“Some of the best demigods have gotten their start by blowing up toilets.”</i><br><br>He's just as swoony as ever.<br><br>And of course,who can forget that sudden twist in the end where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ LEO AND CALYPSO CAME BACK <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>It was like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462492069ra/19004642.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>YEEEES GUUURL YEEEES.<br><br>And Rick Riordan?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462492069ra/19004643.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1390825138" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1390825138" />
    <a title="Silanur" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21110625-silanur"><img alt="Silanur" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453787262p2/21110625.jpg" /></a>
