<div id="review_2282233161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2282233161" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2282233161?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282233161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9763513541234672418">Don’t you just love it when a new spin-off series in a previously established world lives up to the <b>nostalgia</b> of your childhood? Because I do! I clearly remember coming across a small paperback, titled <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6576836-the-lightning-thief' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lightning Thief</a>, sold on a small table of books at age 9. I will never forget that moment as it rekindled my love of mythology, which happened to be the tales that I was raised on. Percy Jackson was a fundamental aspect of my childhood, which makes my enjoyment of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859-the-hidden-oracle' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hidden Oracle</a> that much s</span>
  <span id="freeText9763513541234672418" style="display:none">Don’t you just love it when a new spin-off series in a previously established world lives up to the <b>nostalgia</b> of your childhood? Because I do! I clearly remember coming across a small paperback, titled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6576836-the-lightning-thief" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a>, sold on a small table of books at age 9. I will never forget that moment as it rekindled my love of mythology, which happened to be the tales that I was raised on. Percy Jackson was a fundamental aspect of my childhood, which makes my enjoyment of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859-the-hidden-oracle" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a> that much sweeter.<br><br>Meet <b>Apollo</b>, the Sun God:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480713587ra/21342607.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is the first instalment in a new series centred around Apollo, who has just been cast out of Olympus, after having incurred Zeus’ wrath. Apollo finds himself in a dustbin with the appearance of a pimply and flabby teenager, named <b>Lester Papadopoulos</b>. To make matters worse, he no longer has any of his godly strength or powers. Needless to say, he’s in big trouble! :O Luckily, however, he manages to maintain his brilliant sense of humour (even though he’s being completely serious, it comes across as humour to the reader). <i>“Zeus needed someone to blame, so of course he’d picked the handsomest, most talented, most popular god in the pantheon: me.”</i> He’s so funny, snide, <b>vain, selfish, and arrogant</b>. <br><br>Rick Riordan has convincingly portrayed Apollo as a fallen god who needs to learn what it means to be human…that their children aren’t simply <b>replaceable mortals</b> to resolve the gods’ troubles through the completion of quests. Out of all of Riordan’s protagonists, Apollo is nearly matched with Percy Jackson as <b>my favourite narrator</b>. I loved seeing Camp Half-Blood through the eyes of one of the gods, especially one who fathered quite a number of history’s demigods. This book also gave Apollo plenty of opportunities for self-reflection. <i>“I was the worst of the gods, the most guilt-ridden and unfocussed. I couldn’t commit myself to one lover. I couldn’t even choose what to be the god of. I kept shifting from one skill to another – distracted and dissatisfied.”</i> <br><br>Despite his <b>asinine behaviour</b> the majority of the time, he does change over the course of the novel, thus becoming a better version of himself. <i>“Then it occurred to me how many times I had asked for sacrifices, how many heroes I had sent to their deaths. Had they been any less noble and courageous than these <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dryads <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? Yet I had felt no remorse when I sent them off on deadly tasks. I had used them and discarded them, laid waste to their lives to build my own glory. I was no less of a monster than <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nero <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.”</i> I loved seeing Apollo as a <b>protective father</b>, wanting to do right by his demigod offspring. He also took great pride in their achievements, whether it be archery, medicine, or music.<br><br>The best part of this novel, of course, are the <b>cameos</b> from our favourite characters, including Percy Jackson<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, Chiron, Rachel Dare, Will Solace, Nico di Angelo, Leo Valdez, and Calypso <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! <b>PSA:</b> If you haven’t read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40736-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians" rel="nofollow noopener">The Percy Jackson and the Olympians series</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51379-the-heroes-of-olympus" rel="nofollow noopener">The Heroes of Olympus series</a> to their completion, you will get spoiled, whilst reading this. However, if you have no intention of picking those up (which would be depriving yourself of great mythological retellings!), you do not need to read Riordan’s previous series in order to understand and adore this novel. <br><br>For anyone who worried that Rick Riordan’s characters were becoming carbon copies of one another, (considering that he’s written a Greek mythology series, a Roman mythology series, an Egyptian mythology series, as well as a Norse mythology series), you needn’t fear. I truly believe that this is his <b>funniest book yet</b>, and one of the best books that he’s written in quite some time! Bravo, Uncle Rick! I can’t wait to see Apollo again on his next adventure! :D</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9763513541234672418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1409741061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409741061" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409741061?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409741061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14715842115507055385"><i>“Not all monsters were three-ton reptiles with poisonous breath. Many wore human faces.”</i><br/><br/>I just finished <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i>, since I couldn't wait to get my hands on this. Finally I'd find out what happened in a god's head. The result was a little disappointing.<br/><br/>The main reason I didn't like this as much as Riordan's other books was the main character: Apollo. He's pretty self-centered and arrogant, but in a funny and ironic way. Thing is, after a few chapters the fun wears off, but Apollo stay</span>
  <span id="freeText14715842115507055385" style="display:none"><i>“Not all monsters were three-ton reptiles with poisonous breath. Many wore human faces.”</i><br /><br />I just finished <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i>, since I couldn't wait to get my hands on this. Finally I'd find out what happened in a god's head. The result was a little disappointing.<br /><br />The main reason I didn't like this as much as Riordan's other books was the main character: Apollo. He's pretty self-centered and arrogant, but in a funny and ironic way. Thing is, after a few chapters the fun wears off, but Apollo stays as stupid as before. I kept waiting for some character developement. Luckily, in the second half of the book, Apollo grew through his trials and challenges, at least a little.<br /><br />There was lots of great stuff in <i>The Hidden Oracle</i>. Amazing characters like Meg, Will and Nico, and most of all Sally Jackson. I loved returning to Camp Half-Blood once again. And Apollo as an openly bi (or pan?) sexual character in a children's and YA series is great. But I still caught myself skimming parts. There was just too much that bothered me.<br /><br />There's that thing where authors keep writing about their world, not knowing when to stop (yeah you got me, I'm talking about a certain Shadowhunters author). But I don't get that feeling about Rick Riordan's books.<br />What does tire me out however, is that after the Titan War and Gaea awakening, there should be another threat to this world, possibly even more sinister and dangerous. Seems unlikely to me.<br />And last but not least we have Leo Valdez. And I don't like Leo Valdez. And I don't care for Leo Valdez. And I was happy that he was no big part of this book. But that's where my luck runs out. Seems like he's going to be a main character in the sequel.<br /><br />I doubt that I can handle both Apollo and Leo in <i>The Dark Prophecy (The Trials of Apollo, #2)</i>. So I think it's understadable that I'm not too keen on continuing this series. I'll decide when its release date will come closer.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14715842115507055385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1389780256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389780256" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389780256?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389780256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13658388821900665661"><b>Edit 08/10/15</b><br/><br/>We have more details on THE HIDDEN ORACLE! (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.hypable.com/rick-riordan-percy-jackson-trials-apollo/'>http://www.hypable.com/rick-riordan-p...</a>) I think I might just die right here. APOLLO. APOLLO!!! Only my favourite god from the PJO world. I am <i>so</i> ready for bad haikus and humour. <span id="freeTextContainer18433380400161559298">3.5 stars ⭐️<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Is anything sadder than the sound of a god hitting a pile of garbage bags?</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>The Hidden Oracle</b> is the first book in The Trials Of Apollo series which follows the Olympian god <b>Apollo</b> after he has been stripped of his immortality as well as all his powers, and has been banished to earth by Zeus as a punishment.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Zeus needed someone to blame, so of course he’d picked the handsomest, most talented, most popular god in the pantheon: me.</i>

  <span id="freeText18433380400161559298" style="display:none">3.5 stars ⭐️<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Is anything sadder than the sound of a god hitting a pile of garbage bags?</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>The Hidden Oracle</b> is the first book in The Trials Of Apollo series which follows the Olympian god <b>Apollo</b> after he has been stripped of his immortality as well as all his powers, and has been banished to earth by Zeus as a punishment.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Zeus needed someone to blame, so of course he’d picked the handsomest, most talented, most popular god in the pantheon: me.</i>
</b><br /><br />* * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * *<br /><br />I don't know what to say about this book. It wasn't bad, but I couldn't connect to any of the characters. The reason I could finally finish this is because I switched to the audio version after around 60%. <br /><br />I love buddy-reading this author's books with my sister, and we started a buddy-read for this too. However, she finished this in less than a week while it took almost <i>20 days</i> for me to be done with this.<br /><br /><b>Rick Riordan</b> is one of my favourite authors, and I absolutely love the two other series I read by him, but this one just didn't do it for me.</span>

<div id="review_1410769935" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410769935" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564510350p2/8563233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410769935?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141363912" href="/book/show/26881479-the-hidden-oracle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2016-rockmytbr-challenge">2016-rockmytbr-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410769935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15080650584874111964">Right, so I've just finished my final exams, and will be graduating uni in a few weeks. My degree is combined history and ancient history, and since I was young, tales about mythology have intrigued me, either reading the originals, or adaptations/retellings. Rick Riordan quickly became one of my favourite authors about five years ago, when I discovered the Percy Jackson series, and since then I've loved anything by him.<br/><br/>When I first heard that Riordan would be returning to the world of Percy Jac</span>
  <span id="freeText15080650584874111964" style="display:none">Right, so I've just finished my final exams, and will be graduating uni in a few weeks. My degree is combined history and ancient history, and since I was young, tales about mythology have intrigued me, either reading the originals, or adaptations/retellings. Rick Riordan quickly became one of my favourite authors about five years ago, when I discovered the Percy Jackson series, and since then I've loved anything by him.<br /><br />When I first heard that Riordan would be returning to the world of Percy Jackson, after the end of the Heroes of Olympus series, I immediately added it to my wishlist. Taking place about six months after the end of Blood of Olympus, the god Apollo has angered his father and is punished by being turned mortal, landing, quite literally, in a dumpster in New York. He realises he needs help to get to Camp Half Blood, so tries to find Percy, with the help of his new friend, Meg. Once he manages to get to the camp, he finds out that life isn't going to be quite as easy as expected, as the Oracle of Delphi, and for that matter, all the Oracles, has grown silent, and campers are going missing on a weekly basis. Sinister forces appear to be at work, and with the gods no longer communicating with their children, it's up to Apollo to save the day.<br /><br />I loved the way Apollo was portrayed. Yes, he was a bit similar to Percy, but also had his own distinctive voice. He could be whiny at times, but that's down to his being a god for thousands of years, and having a sense of entitlement that he's been used to. He didn't really click with the campers at first, especially with his children, cause that was a bit awkward, but over the course of the book, his character really grew and developed, and I can't wait to see more of that in the future instalments.<br /><br />If you've read Riordan's other new series, Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard, this book takes place at roughly the same time, so I can see some overlap coming in the future. With Percy having a cameo part in this book, and Annabeth in The Sword of Summer, I happy we can see how they develop further, without them being the main characters of the story. The secondary characters, some of whom we've met before, added to the plot, and I, like many others, was overjoyed to see the Solangelo ship sailing! Meg, though younger than most of the others, was like a breath of fresh air. She didn't take any stick from Apollo, and her own back story and development was as good as Apollo's. Their friendship was a bit reminiscent of Percy and Annabeth in the start, but I don't think I can see them developing into a relationship, because of the age thing - though you never know.<br /><br />For me, my favourite era of Ancient History is Roman - the Late Republic and early Empire - so the development of the Triumvirate storyline intrigues me. Really, I'm just excited for the next book, even though that's going to be months away. If you've enjoyed Riordan's other books, this is one for you to pick up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15080650584874111964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14751931872173634007"><i>Ah it was so nice to be back in Rick's universe!</i><br/>While I thought this was <b>very fun and entertaining</b>, and I LOVED getting to read about what everyone was up to, this was probably my <i>least</i> favorite of his so far. It was still great, I'm just saying in comparison to The Percy Jackson and the Olympians series and the Heroes of Olympus series. I also liked Magnus Chase a little more. I think the biggest reason was <u>Apollo</u>. Don't get me wrong, he was ridiculous and made me laugh, but he just couldn't li</span>
  <span id="freeText14751931872173634007" style="display:none"><i>Ah it was so nice to be back in Rick's universe!</i><br />While I thought this was <b>very fun and entertaining</b>, and I LOVED getting to read about what everyone was up to, this was probably my <i>least</i> favorite of his so far. It was still great, I'm just saying in comparison to The Percy Jackson and the Olympians series and the Heroes of Olympus series. I also liked Magnus Chase a little more. I think the biggest reason was <u>Apollo</u>. Don't get me wrong, he was ridiculous and made me laugh, but he just couldn't live up to Percy and the gang. However, I'm SUPER excited to read the next one now that I know <b>who</b> Apollo will be going on this next journey with!!<br /><br />What did you all think? </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N96EBWw6kkLUEkgA1oAjMnw8kXnPW2a09rVvvWSzCXEN+O3X12RbKnM5/GEhdSntqmN2sQHW6NOtyykMqfD76w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
